<name>Sean Schluntz< /name><text>This is an interesting place, it's setup like a fancy / high end restaurant and charges the prices you would expect for one but is also accepting of the people who are camping in the RV or Tent sites. It's nice that it's open like that.

They start you off with a nice bagett / sourdough loaf and garlic butter  I had Cesar salad and Cioppino and my wife the clam chowder, corn risotto and crab cakes.

The salad was good but in one of those strange fancy / not moments I wasn't offered ground pepper with it - I made due with the pepper on the table. The Cioppino had a flavorful but watery broth with a fair helping of seafood but it was all a bit overcooked (tough shrimp, fish that would have been dry if not in broth). I wasn't dissapointed, it wasn't bad, it was just average.

My wife reported the chowder was also on the thin side but had good flavor and she really enjoyed the crab cakes and risotto.

The restaurant has a full bad and I found the local speciality generous in size and surprisingly inexpensive as far as mixed drinks go.

I've been here before and have never had a bad meal (they have mad good cobblers in the past) and if you are already here it's a nice place to eat. I don't think I would make it a destination. Though, ~25 miles up the coast are quite a few other options, probably the same south of here.<//text>< Pics>

4< /Rating>
<Text>The ideal place to eat is one where the person or persons spending to eat there, can and will get the very illusive money‚Äôs worth from the place. Delicias Peruanas seem to comprehend how important is this concept. A family operation in the full sense of the word, they served us two delicious ceviche mixtos ($12 each?) and a very good looking fried fish with rice and fresh salsa ($14?), which one of my lovely female companions ate in its entirety. Also the special of the day for $8.50 which included a drink ü•É (strawberry water cold), a home made soup, and a chicken stew (Peruvian style). Prices are average for the area, and the food very well made. The lovely female owner/operator was a delight, efficient and courteous. The father and son team (father main cook) completed this well oiled team. Yes, we paid around $58 with gratuity, but we left satisfied, and at the end of the day, isn‚Äôt that what is all about? 4 Stars.< /Text>< pics>

<Time>1527477548181< /Time><Rate>4< /Rate><text>Kind of hole-in-the-wall place for Peruvian fare in Lake Forest, not some fancy diner for trendy people. It's the kind of place where people go to savor food that they grew up with, prepared in as close a possible to grandma's cooking. The paella is prepared differently compared to the Spanish or Mexican version, garnished with a different set of herbs. The chicken grilled with the flatiron is something to behold, so tender on the inside and crispy on the outside. If you are adventurous, they offer grilled cow heart for your taking. Parking is free. Accepts all major credit cards except American Express.< /text>< pics>

<user>108950671193154307598</user>< pictures>
None< /pictures>
<Rating>4<//Rating><gmap_id>0x80dce859add6886f:0xa1e8dca9601894d7<//gmap_id>< Time>
1450815874755<//Time>
< review>
Delicias Peruanas is a family-operated Peruvian restaurant in Lake Forest. The family is Japanese-Peruvian, with father in the kitchen, mother behind the counter, and son as the sever. Japanese and Peruvian may sound like an unusual combination, but Japanese-Peruvians represent 0.3% of the population in Peru. During the Sino-Japanese War in the late 1800's, the economy of Japan suffered and it produced a surplus of local farmers. Peru welcomed the immigration of hard working Japanese farmers. These Japanese immigrants combined their native recipes with Peru's favorable fishing environment and the rice imported by the Spanish, giving rise to unique Japanese-inspired-Peruvian dishes prepared with novel cooking styles (Nikkei cuisine).

Although the chef and son at Delicias Peruanas have Japanese blood and possess an Asian appearance, they speak fluent Spanish. The chef cooks authentic Peruvian dishes (with Asian flair) and the server Roberto is competent in describing the differences in each dish.

During lunch, a $8 special is available, which is affordable given that it consists of a selection among 4 Peruvian-inspired entrees with generous portion, a soup/salad, a citrus concentrate beverage, and bread with aji sauce. For a light eater, this can be equivalent to two meals.

The soup was similar to a garden vegetable soup but also resembled a clear version of an Italian minestrone. Zucchini, celery, cabbage, lima beans, and cilantro were found. The bread was standard but the spicy aji sauce was remarkable. The citrus beverage was a refreshing juice with passion fruit flavors, appropriate for the summertime.

The main course that I ordered was the estofado de pollo. Two pieces of tender chicken (thigh and leg) were garnished with pepper, herbs, and mild spices. The chicken was placed in a thin tomato sauce and served over a bed of rice, two pieces of potato, and sliced red onions. I recommend this dish to those who prefer wet food since estofado de pollo is a chicken stew over rice. For those who prefer dry food, I recommend the pescado frito (pan fried tilapia) dish available on the lunch special menu. The dishes are not fully representative of traditional Peruvian cuisine, it's fits the Peruvian-American fusion tastes.

While I waited for my lunch, I observed the kitchen and discovered that the chef cooking with an open fire and a flambe technique. I don't think every dish is prepared this way, but it was quite a sight to see the chef hold a small pan engulfed with 3' high flames!

Delicias Peruanas is no longer a hidden hole in the wall. Word has gotten out about this gem in Lake Forest, so don't be surprised to encounter a lunch crowd. I am eager to return soon and try the other $8 lunch specials.<//review>

I personally respect that as this type of honesty and integrity is rare in this industry and is well worth the wait.

< review>
The service and the facility is fine, but this facility has a very strange rule that no exchange tickets.  We bought tickets online, through my cell phone, and it didn‚Äôt allow me to pick seats.  The computer picked the front row to watch a Ballet show, which is going to be a torture of the neck.  We didn‚Äôt realize the seating situation until we arrived at our seats.  Went to the box office and asked if we could exchange to seats in the very back since there are seats not selling.  They said no.  They asked me to purchase additional four seats!   Have been to many different facilities and theatres, and this is the first time I was asked to pay additional money!   So if you order online, don‚Äôt do it through cell phone, and pick your own seats, don‚Äôt let the computer do it.  The computer or the system setup is very dumb!</review>

<Review>This is a nice little theater, on the small side of venues. There isn't really a bad seat, unless it's in the balcony (we haven't been seated there). We won tickets from KPRI for Colin Hay, and had a good time.
Know that it will take you a little while to get there, because it is way out on the outskirts of Poway. It also is connected to a High School, so parking for a Friday night performance can be hairy if there's a game that night. Be prepared for a little bit of a hike.
The theater offers a pre-performance buffet package for the weekend shows. We haven't experienced that, we usually eat at Santorini which is about a mile away and very good.<//Review><Pics>None< /Pics><resp>None</resp><Gmap_id>0x80dbfa8270c4b757:0xdd9c33dd7ea4df7b</Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

<Date>1553995049481</Date>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<text>My family and I went here to use our Fun Cards we got for Christmas. We had a BLAST! My family and I got to enjoy Lazer Tag, Go-Karts racing (my children drove on the smaller kid carts and then were passengers on the big karts), mini golf, paddle boats, a bumper chair ride, the batting cages and arcade games.

For lunch we had the family pack which had 10 slices of pizza, 4 drinks some wings and a few celery sticks.

My family ended up spending 6 hours here and I know my children will be asking to go back here soon.

<text>Great place to take your kids for a birthday party!  We brought our daughter here for her 7th birthday.

We purchased the ultimate birthday party package.

All of the kids enjoyed unlimited rides on the go karts, bumper cars, paddle boats, miniature golf, and laser tag!  Plus, each received a card good for $15 of arcade play.

The staff was fantastic! Everyone was very attentive and patient with our gaggle of kids running around.

The kids enjoyed pizza and cake. For the adults we were able to purchase turkey sandwich trays, boneless buffalo wings, boneless BBQ wings, green salad.

Unlimited soft drinks were included, and the adults were able to purchase a variety of draft beers if wanted.

Overall, everyone had a good time.

And, there's something really magical about not having to clean up after the party!</text>< username>

< review>
First, I did not drive so access to public transportation is crucial. The public bus stop was on the main street leaving us to walk three blocks. I was satisfied with the walking distance. My niece and nephew enjoyed themselves completely despite riding two attractions the entire time we were there. They were too old for the padde boats. I thought for sure they would be interested in the rock climbing wall and maybe the miniature golf but I was wrong. Speed and driving captured their attention so the bumper cars and the go carts were the only two attractions that held their fascination. I spent $75 for a ticket card which is swiped at each attraction. The place gives additional funds so I had a total of $120 to spend. My niece and nephew were also able to play some of the games in the arcade area. I spent cash for pizza and drinks another $23.00. The place was crowded hosting many children's parties. But the longest wait happen to be for the go carts. When you are in the public, expect some wait time which for all of us waiting in line was fine while we talked while watching the people and the activity.</review>

< Text>
First, I did not drive so access to public transportation is crucial. The public bus stop was on the main street leaving us to walk three blocks. I was satisfied with the walking distance. My niece and nephew enjoyed themselves completely despite riding two attractions the entire time we were there. They were too old for the padde boats. I thought for sure they would be interested in the rock climbing wall and maybe the miniature golf but I was wrong. Speed and driving captured their attention so the bumper cars and the go carts were the only two attractions that held their fascination. I spent $75 for a ticket card which is swiped at each attraction. The place gives additional funds so I had a total of $120 to spend. My niece and nephew were also able to play some of the games in the arcade area. I spent cash for pizza and drinks another $23.00. The place was crowded hosting many children's parties. But the longest wait happen to be for the go carts. When you are in the public, expect some wait time which for all of us waiting in line was fine while we talked while watching the people and the activity.<//Text>

<date>1522709263421< /date><rate>1<//rate>< text>
Besides the staff I encountered who were all very helpful, happy and upbeat, this place wasn't worth the 30 miles I drove to get there.  I took my two and seven year old and their 10 year old cousin. With all the weight and height limitations they weren't able to ride anything together. We waited at two different "ride/attractions" for quite some time before anyone came to let the kids on. It wasn't busy, it just seemed like no one was manning their posts. Not a place for toddlers! I did more chasing him around trying to make sure he wasn't getting into anything he wasn't supposed to, wich was EVERYTHING. The paddle boats we're not what I was expecting, maybe because past experiences I have had we're never like that. They are basically oversized rubber duckies the kids paddle like a bicycle in an oversized jacuzzi. I'm not saying this place is horrible. If I lived closer to it and it was a little cheaper, it might be a go to place once every six months or so. The mini golf was cool. I'm just saying don't take little kids. Don't drive to far to get there, it's not worth that.<//text>
